THE IRON SULFIDE AND OXYGEN MIXTURE LIKELY IGNITED, RESULTING IN A FLASH FIRE THAT EXITED THE MAN-WAY DOOR AND CAUSED BURN INJURIES TO THE TWO WORKERS. 911 WAS IMMEDIATELY NOTIFIED AND EMS ARRIVED ON SITE APPROXIMATELY 10 MINUTES LATER. THE TWO INJURED CONTRACTORS WERE TRANSPORTED BY EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICES FOR FURTHER TREATMENT. ONCE THE AREA WAS DEEMED SAFE, THE MAN-WAY DOOR WAS REINSTALLED TO PREVENT FURTHER OXYGEN-IRON SULFIDE MIXTURES FROM FORMING. THE SEPARATOR WAS ALSO FILLED WITH WATER USING LOW PRESSURE TO MITIGATE POTENTIAL IGNITION/OXYGEN INTERACTION. TO MITIGATE RECURRENCE, TARGA INTENDS TO (I) DEVELOP WRITTEN PROCEDURES FOR ASSESSING/MANAGEMENT OF IRON SULFIDE AND (II) TRAIN ITS EMPLOYEES ON IRON SULFIDE HAZARDS, ASSOCIATED RISKS AND MITIGATION MEASURES. THE INVESTIGATION REMAINS ONGOING AT THIS TIME."

THERE WAS A HAMMER UNION CONNECTION IN THIS PIPING WHICH WAS FOUND TO BE LOOSE WITH ONLY MINIMAL THREAD ENGAGEMENT. WHEN THE PRV WAS TRIGGERED IT ALLOWED GAS TO ESCAPE FROM THE HAMMER UNION ENGULFING THE ENGINE. THIS GAS IGNITED WHEN GAS MOVED DOWNWIND (SOUTHWEST) AND THEN ALLOWED THE FUEL SOURCE TO CONTINUE TO SUSTAIN THE FIRE.       TO PREVENT THIS FROM OCCURRING IN THE FUTURE, ENERGY TRANSFER HAS SINCE PURCHASED THE OTHER 2 NOVA RENTAL UNITS AT THIS LOCATION.  BOTH REMAINING UNITS HAVE UNDERGONE MAJOR OVERHAULS TO ADDRESS ANY FUTURE VIBRATION ISSUES."

THERE WILL ALSO BE SOAP TESTS (LEAK TESTS) CONDUCTED ON INITIAL STARTUP TO ENSURE ALL PROCESS CONNECTIONS ARE NOT LEAKING ONCE THE SYSTEM IS PRESSURIZED. THIS CAUSED THE LINE TO OVERPRESSURE AND RUPTURE. WHEN THE LINE RUPTURED 5 MILES AWAY IT KNOCKED DOWN GATHERING COMPRESSION. THE WES OPERATIONS PERSONNEL RECOGNIZED HIS ERROR AND RETURNED TO THE VALVE SET TO CLOSE THE INCORRECT VALVE, THEN RESPONDED TO THE COMPRESSION ALARMS, UNKNOWINGLY HAVING RUPTURED THE LINE, 5 MILES AWAY.    AT 12:15 PM ON 12/16/2024 A DIFFERENT WES EMPLOYEE, ENROUTE TO TROUBLESHOOT THE COMPRESSOR ISSUE, OBSERVED A PIPELINE RELEASE ON WESTERN MIDSTREAM'S 14 INCH POLY LINE. THE WES EMPLOYEE IMMEDIATELY REQUESTED ADDITIONAL PERSONNEL TO ISOLATE THE LINE. COMPRESSOR SHUTDOWNS UPSTREAM AND DOWNSTREAM OF THE RUPTURE ISOLATED THE GAS FLOW WITHIN FIVE MINUTES. THE NEAREST VALVES TO THE RUPTURE SITE WERE CLOSED MANUALLY BY WES OPERATORS AND THE LINE WAS FLAT WITHIN 30 MINUTES OF THE LEAK BEING DISCOVERED. NOTIFICATIONS WERE MADE INTERNALLY SO THAT DATA COULD BE COLLECTED TO DETERMINE GAS LOSS, AND EXTERNALLY TO AFFECTED UTILITIES, OPERATORS, AND PRODUCERS IMPACTED BY THE LINE RELEASE. THE LINE REMAINED OUT OF SERVICE UNTIL AN INCIDENT INVESTIGATION WAS COMPLETED, THE UTILITIES AND THIRD-PARTY INFRASTRUCTURE WERE REPAIRED, A HAZARD ANALYSIS WAS PERFORMED, AND THE 14 INCH POLY LINE WAS REPAIRED BY REPLACEMENT SECTION.     WESTERN MIDSTREAM PERFORMED A REVIEW OF SIMILAR LARGE DIAMETER HIGH TO LOW PRESSURE CONNECTIONS THROUGHOUT THE FIELD. SIX ADDITIONAL LOCATIONS WERE IDENTIFIED WITH SIMILAR DESIGNS. ALL WERE ELIMINATED BY REMOVING THE CONNECTION ENTIRELY.  TRAINING WAS COMPLETED THROUGH A SAFETY STAND DOWN AND INCIDENT REVIEW."

ONCE THE AREA WAS DEEMED SAFE, REMEDIATION EFFORTS BEGAN UTILIZING A VACUUM TRUCK TO DISPOSE OF STANDING LIQUID IN THE LEAK AREA. THE LEAK OCCURRED ON A ""FUTURE HOT TAP"" FITTING INSTALLED IN THE PIPELINE. THIS FITTING IS A SHORT STEEL SEGMENT INSTALLED BETWEEN 2 SECTIONS OF POLYETHYLENE PIPELINE AND INCLUDED A 3 INCH LINE COMING OUT OF THE BOTTOM OF THE PIPE AND A 12 INCH ""T"" COMING FROM THE TOP OF THE PIPE WITH BOTH TERMINATING ABOVE GROUND. THE 3 INCH SERVED AS AN ADDITIONAL BLOWDOWN POINT ON THE PIPELINE AND THE 12 INCH COULD BE UTILIZED TO INSTALL FUTURE PIPELINE TIE-INS VIA HOT TAPPING. IN ORDER TO PREVENT AND MITIGATE RECURRENCE TARGA IS IN THE PROCESS OF REMOVING ALL SUCH FITTINGS THAT ARE FOUND TO BE INSTALLED IN THE GATHERING SYSTEM AND WILL NOT BE INSTALLED ON ANY NEW PIPELINES. ADDITIONALLY, TARGA UTILIZES AERIAL PATROL SURVEYS TO MITIGATE THE MAGNITUDE OF LEAKS BY DETECTING THEM EARLIER."

NATURAL FORCE DAMAGE	HEAVY RAINS/FLOODS																																																					HEAVY RAINS/FLOODS		FLOTATION				YES				YES	SEVERE FLASH FLOODING																																																																																																																																																																																																						DANIEL STAHL	PIPELINE INTEGRITY ENGINEER	daniel.stahl@bhegts.com	3042666062		SHAWNIE DAVIS	shawnie.davis@bhegts.com	304-203-2158	MIKE FERGUSON	MANAGER - PIPELINE INTEGRITY	8032600335	mike.ferguson@bhegts.com	"THE RESPONSE TO THIS INCIDENT WAS COMPLICATED BY THE PREVAILING WEATHER CONDITIONS. AT THE TIME OF THE INCIDENT, KANAWHA COUNTY WAS EXPERIENCING SEVERE FLASH FLOODING SPECIFICALLY IN AREAS NEAR SLAUGHTERS CREEK AND A STATE OF EMERGENCY WAS DECLARED BY THE STATE OF WEST VIRGINIA ON 8/28/23. GAS CONTROL RECEIVED INITIAL NOTIFICATION OF THIS INCIDENT ON 8/28/23 AT APPROXIMATELY 08:00 BASED ON A PRESSURE DROP AT CORNWELL COMPRESSOR STATION (WHICH IS UPSTREAM OF WHERE THE INCIDENT OCCURRED ON TL-263) AS INDICATED BY THE SCADA SYSTEM. GAS CONTROL HAD EARLIER BEEN NOTIFIED BY DIVERSIFIED ENERGY AT APPROXIMATELY 06:30 THAT A PIPELINE OPERATED BY DIVERSIFIED ENERGY THAT IS CONNECTED TO TL-263 AT SLAUGHTERS CREEK M&R (WHICH IS LOCATED IN PROXIMITY TO SLAUGHTERS CREEK) HAD ALSO EXPERIENCED A PRESSURE DROP AND IT WAS LATER DETERMINED THAT THE PIPELINE OPERATED BY DIVERSIFIED ENERGY EXPERIENCED A FULL GUILLOTINE BREAK AS A RESULT OF THE SEVERE FLASH FLOODING. THAT FULL GUILLOTINE BREAK OCCURRED AT A POINT IN TIME BEFORE THE INCIDENT OCCURRED ON TL-263. TL-263 IS A TYPE R (REGULATORY REPORTING) GATHERING PIPELINE AND HAS A MAXIMUM ALLOWABLE OPERATING PRESSURE OF 274 PSIG. AT THE TIME OF THE INCIDENT, THE OPERATING PRESSURE ON TL-263 WAS 240 PSIG AND TL-263 WAS FLOWING GAS. OPERATIONS PERSONNEL WERE PREVENTED BY LOCAL EMERGENCY RESPONDERS FROM BEING ABLE TO ACCESS CERTAIN ABOVEGROUND FACILITIES (INCLUDING SLAUGHTERS CREEK M&R) ASSOCIATED WITH TL-263 BECAUSE OF THE SEVERE FLASH FLOODING. WHEN IT WAS SAFE TO DO SO, OPERATIONS PERSONNEL BEGAN ISOLATING THE SECTION OF TL-263 CONTAINING SLAUGHTERS CREEK M&R. OPERATIONS PERSONNEL MANUALLY CLOSED VALVE N AT CHELYAN COMPRESSOR STATION AT APPROXIMATELY 10:15 WHICH IS UPSTREAM OF WHERE THE INCIDENT OCCURRED ON TL-263 AND CONNECTS TL-263 TO TL-570. OPERATIONS PERSONNEL MANUALLY CLOSED VALVE D AT LOUP CREEK COMPRESSOR STATION AT APPROXIMATELY 11:00 AM WHICH IS DOWNSTREAM OF WHERE THE INCIDENT OCCURRED ON TL-263 AND DOWNSTREAM OF THE FEED ON TL-263 FROM EASTERN AMERICAN ENERGY AT EASTERN AMERICAN GATE. OPERATIONS PERSONNEL ARRIVED AT THE SITE WHERE THE INCIDENT OCCURRED ON TL-263 AT APPROXIMATELY 15:00 AT WHICH POINT IT WAS REALIZED THAT TL-263 HAD SUFFERED A FULL GUILLOTINE BREAK AT THE ABOVEGROUND CROSSING OF SLAUGHTERS CREEK. IT IS BELIEVED THAT THIS WAS CAUSED BY FLOATING DEBRIS THAT WAS ADRIFT AS A RESULT OF THE SEVERE FLASH FLOODING. OPERATIONS PERSONNEL MANUALLY CLOSED VALVE A AT THE WHITE OAKS RECEIVER AT APPROXIMATELY 17:00 WHICH IS DOWNSTREAM OF WHERE THE INCIDENT OCCURRED ON TL-263 AND UPSTREAM OF VALVE D AT LOUP CREEK COMPRESSOR STATION AND THE FEED ON TL-263 FROM EASTERN AMERICAN ENERGY AT EASTERN AMERICAN GATE. THE CLOSURE OF VALVE A AT THE WHITE OAKS RECEIVER COMPLETED THE ISOLATION OF THE SECTION OF TL-263 CONTAINING THE INCIDENT. INITIAL TELEPHONIC NOTIFICATION WAS MADE TO THE NATIONAL RESPONSE CENTER ON 8/28/23 AT 20:49. THE NATIONAL RESPONSE CENTER ASSIGNED INCIDENT REPORT #1377546 TO THE INITIAL NOTIFICATION OF THE INCIDENT. A FOLLOW UP TELEPHONIC NOTIFICATION WAS MADE TO THE NATIONAL RESPONSE CENTER ON 8/30/23 AT 17:30 TO CONFIRM THE INITIAL TELEPHONIC NOTIFICATION AND UPDATE THE VOLUME OF UNINTENTIONAL GAS LOSS. THE NATIONAL RESPONSE CENTER ASSIGNED INCIDENT REPORT #1377726 TO THE FOLLOW UP TELEPHONIC NOTIFICATION. THE FOLLOWING REMEDIAL ACTIONS WERE COMPLETED: THE ENTIRE LENGTH OF TL-263 WAS PATROLLED VIA HELICOPTER WHEN WEATHER CONDITIONS ALLOWED ON 8/30/23, THE SECTION OF TL-263 WHERE THE INCIDENT OCCURRED WAS CAPPED OFF, AND FLOW WAS RESUMED ON TL-263 VIA THE CONNECTION BETWEEN TL-263 AND TL-570 AT BLACK EAGLE JUNCTION WHICH IS DOWNSTREAM OF WHERE THE INCIDENT OCCURRED ON TL-263 BUT UPSTREAM OF VALVE A AT THE WHITE OAKS RECEIVER. FOLLOWING COMPLETION OF THE REMEDIAL ACTIONS, TL-263 WAS RETURNED TO SERVICE ON 9/15/23 AT 05:48."

MANAGER	405-576-8230	jimmy.cross@energytransfer.com	"ON 5/26/2023 AT APPROXIMATELY 8:30AM, TRIANGLE TRUCK DRIVER NOTICED GAS SMELL WHILE DRIVING HIS PIPELINE DRIP ROUTE. AS HE CONTINUED TO DRIVE, THE ENGINE BEGAN TO OVER REV. REALIZING WHAT WAS HAPPENING, HE EXITED TRUCK, AND MOVED TO A SAFE AREA. THE GAS IGNITED CAUSING A FIRE. THE TRUCK DRIVER NOTIFIED HIS SUPERVISOR, WHO THEN CONTACTED ENERGY TRANSFER OPERATIONS MANAGER TO NOTIFY HIM OF THE EVENT. THE THIRD PARTY ALSO CONTACTED THE FIRE DEPARTMENT. THE ENERGY TRANSFER OPERATIONS MANAGER NOTIFIED FIELD OPERATIONS SUPERVISOR TO INVESTIGATE THE EVENT AT APPROXIMATELY 8:42AM. THE PIPELINE IS IN A COMMON PIPELINE CORRIDOR, AND IN AN AREA WHERE ENERGY TRANSFER HAS LEASED PIPELINES. ALTHOUGH THE PIPELINE OWNERSHIP WAS UNKNOWN, ENERGY TRANSFER FIELD OPERATIONS SUPERVISOR CONTACTED FIELD PERSONNEL TO START SHUTTING IN THE 909 STINNETT 24' AT 8:43AM. THE FIRE DEPARTMENT ARRIVED ON SCENE AT APPROXIMATELY 9:02AM. OPERATIONS PERSONNEL CLOSED THE PIPELINE VALVES MANUALLY, THE DOWNSTREAM VALVE AT 9:30AM AND THE UPSTREAM VALVE AT 9:45AM. AT APPROXIMATELY 11:00AM OPERATIONS DETERMINED THE PIPELINE WAS AN ENERGY TRANSFER ASSET. THE NRC WAS NOTIFIED AT 11:06AM. THE FIRE BURNED OUT AT APPROXIMATELY 1:20PM.   AFTER A MULTITUDE OF WEATHER DELAYS, REPAIRS ON THE 909 STINNETT 24' WERE COMPLETED ON JUNE 28, 2023. THE REPAIR CONSISTED OF A PIPE REPLACEMENT WITH (SDR) ELEVEN POLY PIPE. OPERATIONS PLACED THE PIPELINE BACK INTO SERVICE ON JULY 6, 2023. THE PIPELINE HAD ASPHALT COATING WITH NO INDICATIONS OF DISBONDING. THE WALL THICKNESSES RANGED FROM .276 TO .295 INCHES. COMPANY INTEGRITY AND CORROSION PERSONNEL CONDUCTED INTERNAL VISUAL EXAMINATIONS OF PIPE SECTIONS REMOVED BOTH UPSTREAM AND DOWNSTREAM OF THE LEAK LOCATION. INTERNAL CORROSION WAS DETERMINED TO BE THE LEAK CAUSE. BACTERIAL LAB TESTS WERE PERFORMED. THE TEST RESULTS RECEIVED BACK BY THE COMPANY ON JULY 24, 2023. TESTING SHOWED THAT THE INTERNAL CORROSION WAS DUE TO SULFATE AND ACID PRODUCING BACTERIA. TO DETER REOCCURRENCE, THE COMPANY WILL BE INJECTING A CORROSION INHIBITOR, AS WELL AS ADDING COUPON MONITORING."

ROUTINE MAINTENANCE																																																							BRYAN ROBISON	PIPELINE COMPLIANCE SPECIALIST	brobison@targaresources.com	8179440617					GREGG JOHNSON	DIRECTOR PIPELINE COMPLIANCE	7135841632	gjohnson@targaresources.com	"ON JANUARY 31, 2023, AT APPROXIMATELY 11:52 AM, NEXUS INTEGRITY MANAGEMENT, LLC (""NEXUS"") WAS IN THE PROCESS OF INSTALLING TEST LEADS FROM AN ENTERPRISE PRODUCTS (""ENTERPRISE"") PIPELINE TO A TARGA PIPELINE THAT WAS LOCATED WITHIN THE SAME RIGHT-OF-WAY. DURING THE WORK ACTIVITIES AN INCIDENT OCCURRED RESULTING IN ONE FATALITY OF A NEXUS EMPLOYEE AND INJURING TWO OTHER NEXUS EMPLOYEES. TARGA'S PIPELINE WAS DAMAGED DURING THE EVENT. ONE TARGA EMPLOYEE AND ONE ENTERPRISE EMPLOYEE WERE ON LOCATION WHEN THE EVENT OCCURRED.    NEXUS WAS HIRED TO INSTALL TEST LEADS CONNECTING TWO ENTERPRISE PIPELINES TO TWO TARGA PIPELINES (ONE EIGHT-INCH PIPELINE AND ONE FOUR-INCH PIPELINE) WITHIN A RIGHT-OF-WAY LOCATED AT 28.736804, -99.008283 AFTER TARGA IDENTIFIED STRAY CURRENT NORTH OF THE FOUR-INCH PIPELINE DURING A CATHODIC PROTECTION SURVEY. TARGA ACQUIRED BOTH PIPELINES IN APRIL OF 2022 AND THE PRIOR OPERATOR LISTED THE PIPELINE MATERIAL FOR BOTH PIPELINES AS STEEL IN ITS GIS DATA THAT WAS PROVIDED TO TARGA.   PRIOR TO STARTING PROJECT WORK, NEXUS SUBMITTED A LINE LOCATING REQUEST WITH 811 (TICKET #2352321781). PROJECT WORK BEGAN ON JANUARY 30, 2023 AT THE LOCATION OF THE INCIDENT. ON THAT DAY, NEXUS HYDRO-VACUUM EXCAVATED 12"" X 12"" HOLES TO POSITIVELY IDENTIFY BOTH ENTERPRISE AND BOTH TARGA PIPELINES. NEXUS NEXT WORKED ON THE ENTERPRISE PIPELINES.   ON JANUARY 31, 2023, AT THE SAME LOCATION, NEXUS PLANNED TO INSTALL A TEST LEAD WIRE TO TARGA'S FOUR-INCH PIPELINE THROUGH THE 12"" X 12"" HOLE CREATED ON JANUARY 30, 2023. NEXUS PLANNED TO SAND COATING FROM THE PIPELINE USING A PNEUMATIC SANDER ATTACHED TO AN EXTENSION DEVICE, AND THEN, TO CAD-WELD A TEST LEAD WIRE TO THE TOP OF THE PIPE. BASED ON THE GIS DATA ACQUIRED FROM THE PRIOR OPERATOR, VISUAL INSPECTION OF THE PIPELINE, AND OTHER TESTING, TARGA PERSONNEL CONCLUDED THAT THE PIPELINE WAS STEEL COATED IN FUSION BONDED EPOXY, WHICH IS SIMILAR IN COLOR TO THE MANUFACTURED COLOR OF FIBERSPAR OUTER JACKET AND RESEMBLES FBE COATING. NEXUS SANDED ON THE PIPELINE FOR APPROXIMATELY AN HOUR AND THEN NEXUS INFORMED TARGA THAT IT WAS GOING TO FURTHER EXCAVATE BY HYDROVAC TO GAIN BETTER ACCESS TO THE PIPELINE. AFTER THE INCIDENT, NEXUS INFORMED TARGA THAT IT HAD RETURNED TO SANDING THE PIPELINE AND THE RELEASE OCCURRED.   TARGA'S POST-INCIDENT INVESTIGATION DETERMINED: THE FOUR-INCH PIPELINE WAS FIBERSPAR (COMPOSITE); THE OUTER COLOR OF THE PIPELINE WAS SIMILAR TO FUSION BONDED EPOXY; THE PIPELINE WAS NOT INSTALLED WITH A TRACER WIRE; THE GIS DATA FROM THE PRIOR OPERATOR HAD NOT BEEN UPDATED AS TO THE PIPELINE MATERIAL; NEXUS DID NOT USE ANY EQUIPMENT, TOOLS, PROCEDURES, OR OTHER METHOD TO VERIFY THE PIPELINE COMPOSITION BEFORE STARTING WORK; AND NEXUS SANDED ON THE PIPELINE FOR APPROXIMATELY ONE HOUR AND CONTINUED SANDING WITHOUT EXCAVATING FOR BETTER ACCESS TO THE PIPELINE."

BRAD GENTRY	DIRECTOR OF ENGINEERING - REGULATORY	bgentry@meritagemidstream.com	720.732.2141		BRAD GENTRY	bgentry@meritagemidstream.com	720.732.2141	BRAD GENTRY	DIRECTOR OF ENGINEERING	720.732.2141	bgentry@meritagemidstream.com	"ON DEC 23, 2022 AT 20:31, A FIRE WAS DETECTED ON THE LOW PRESSURE C-2704 SCREW COMPRESSOR UNIT AT THE CROSSBOW GATHERING COMPRESSOR STATION BY LOCAL LEL/FIRE MONITORING DEVICES AND ONSITE OPERATORS. THE LOCAL LEL MONITOR DETECTED FLAMMABLE NATURAL GAS, ALARMED AND BOTH THE LEL AND FIRE EYE SHUTDOWN THE UNIT (E.G. ESD). TWO OPERATORS (INCLUDES CONTRACT OPERATOR) WERE ONSITE AND NOTICED THE FIRE WITHIN THE COMPRESSOR BUILDING AND ONE OF THE OPERATORS HIT THE EMERGENCY SHUTDOWN (ESD) FOR THE SITE. THE OPERATORS SAFELY EVACUATED SITE TO A SAFE MUSTER POINT. AT APPROXIMATELY 20:36, SUPERVISORS/MANAGEMENT AND FIRST RESPONDERS WERE NOTIFIED OF THE EVENTS. THE THUNDER CREEK GAS SERVICE (TCGS) OPERATOR ONSITE SERVED AS INCIDENT COMMAND (IC) UNTIL THE CAMPBELL COUNTY FIRE DEPARTMENT AND TCGS FIELD MANAGEMENT ARRIVED ONSITE AT 21:23 AND 21:28, RESPECTIVELY. THE IC TEAM DETERMINED THAT THE TCGS PERSONNEL COULD SAFELY ENTER THE LOCATION TO FURTHER ISOLATE THE UNIT TO STARVE THE SMALL RESIDUAL FLAMES OF FLAMMABLE GAS. THE TCGS TEAM USED A FIRE EXTINGUISHER TO SAFELY PUT OUT A SMALL FLAME. THE CAMPBELL COUNTY FIRE DEPARTMENT DETERMINED THAT NO FURTHER ASSISTANCE OR OVERSIGHT WAS NEEDED AND WAS RELEASED AT 22:15. THE TCGS SAFETY REPRESENTATIVE ARRIVED ONSITE AT 22:58 AND ASSISTED WITH A COMPLETE SITE WALKDOWN TO ENSURE SAFETY WITH TCGS PERSONNEL. THIS WALKDOWN INCLUDED ASSESSING ALL OTHER COMPRESSOR PACKAGES ONSITE TO DETERMINE IF THEY WERE SAFE FOR OPERATION.     THE PRELIMINARY INVESTIGATION INDICATES THAT THERE WAS A LIKELY FAILURE IN A PIPING COMPONENT DUE TO A FREEZE IN THE DRAIN LINE UNDER THE SUCTION SCRUBBER TO THE SCREW COMPRESSOR PACKAGE. OPERATING DATA INDICATES THAT UNIT AND COMPONENTS DID NOT EXCEED MAOP/MAWP. THE SUSPECTED FAILURE RESULTED IN A GAS LEAK WITHIN THE BUILDING AND THE LIKELY IGNITION SOURCE WAS THE TURBO ON THE ENGINE. AT THE TIME OF INCIDENT, THIS AREA WAS OPERATING AT ABOUT 15 PSIG OF PRESSURE. THE FIRE WAS CONFINED WITHIN THE SMALL BUILDING. THE CAUSE OF THE FREEZE WAS LIKELY DUE TO THE EXTREME WEATHER EVENTS EXPERIENCED IN THE REGION AT THE TIME. THIS STATION HAD ENCOUNTERED SIGNIFICANT DOWNTIME DUE TO LOW GAS VOLUMES FROM THE LOCAL PRODUCTION AREA. DURING THAT DOWNTIME, THE AMBIENT TEMPERATURE WAS SIGNIFICANTLY BELOW ZERO.     IT IS IMPORTANT TO NOTE THAT EACH COMPRESSOR PACKAGE HAS AN INDIVIDUAL BUILDING. THIS INCIDENT DID NOT IMPACT OTHER UNITS, EQUIPMENT, OR PIPING OUTSIDE OF THE PACKAGE. AN INVESTIGATION AND ASSESSMENT TEAM WENT INTO THE UNIT IN THE FOLLOWING DAYS AFTER THE FIRE AND STARTED TO ASSESS ROOT CAUSE AND THE EXTENT OF DAMAGES. DURING THAT PROCESS, THE TEAM REALIZED THAT A SIGNIFICANT AMOUNT OF ELECTRICAL AND ELECTRONIC EQUIPMENT WAS DAMAGED AND WOULD NEED REPLACEMENT. ALSO, SOME PIPING COMPONENTS, DEVICES, AND BUILDING INSULATION/PANELS WOULD REQUIRE REPLACEMENT. ONCE THE TEAM DETERMINED THAT THE COST WOULD EXCEED THE ""INCIDENT REPORTING"" THRESHOLD, AN IMMEDIATE NOTIFICATION WAS MADE TO THE NRC, WITH A 48-HOUR FOLLOW-UP REPORT. TCGS PERSONNEL ALSO COMMUNICATED WITH THE WYOMING DEPARTMENT OF ENVIRONMENTAL QUALITY (WDEQ) AND THE WYOMING PUBLIC SERVICE COMMISSION."

MANAGER REGULATORY COMPLIANCE	4055768230	jimmy.cross@energytransfer.com	"ON 5/17/2022,  AT APPROXIMATELY 19:00, A PRODUCER CONTACTED ENABLE PIPELINE TECHNICIAN CONCERNING A SMALL GAS IMBALANCE BETWEEN HIS METER AND ETC METER. THE METER WAS CHECKED ON THE MORNING OF 5/18/22, BUT NO MEASUREMENT EQUIPMENT ISSUES WERE IDENTIFIED.  PIPELINE TECHNICIAN THEN INVESTIGATED BY PATROLLING THE AO-70 4-INCH PIPELINE RIGHT OF WAY AND DISCOVERED A LEAK AT APPROXIMATELY 11:15.  PIPELINE WAS SHUT IN IMMEDIATELY BY MANUALLY CLOSING THE UPSTREAM AND DOWNSTREAM VALVES AT 11:30 AND 11:50. THE PIPELINE WAS UNCOVERED, AND A SMALL PINHOLE LEAK, APPROXIMATELY 100 THOUSANDTHS IN SIZE, WAS REPAIRED BY INSTALLING A CLAMP. THE PIPELINE WAS RESTARTED AT 19:00 ON 5/18/2022 AND PATROLLED AGAIN, NO ADDITIONAL LEAKS WERE IDENTIFIED.    CLEANUP REMEDIATION BEGAN ON 5/18/2022, ESTIMATED COSTS WERE WELL BELOW THE REPORTING THRESHOLD.  THE COST OF REMEDIATION THEN EXCEEDED THE $122,000 THRESHOLD ON 6/1/2022 AND THE INCIDENT WAS CLASSIFIED AS REPORTABLE AT THAT TIME. NOTIFICATION TO TEXAS RAILROAD COMMISSION OIL & GAS DIVISION WAS PREVIOUSLY MADE ON 5/18/2022 REGARDING THE CONDENSATE SPILL (ENVIRONMENTAL). TELEPHONIC NOTIFICATIONS WERE MADE TO NRC AND TEXAS RAILROAD COMMISSION PIPELINE SAFETY ON 6/1/2022 WHEN THE PIPELINE SAFETY INCIDENT (191.3) CRITERIA WAS MET. REMEDIATION HAS BEEN COMPLETED.    AFTER ET MET WITH PHMSA/PIERZINA ON 9/13/22, INCIDENT REPORT DATES AND TIMES WERE REVISED FOR THE A.4 AND A.13 ENTRIES, PER MR. PIERZINA' S INSTRUCTIONS. THESE REVISIONS PUSHED THE 'EARLIEST LOCAL TIME (24-HR CLOCK) AND DATE AN INCIDENT REPORTING CRITERIA WAS MET' BACK TO 5/17/22, BEFORE THE COST CRITERIA WAS MET."
